<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p>Due to the length of the (ever growing) book list it became necessary to split it in two. Here’s the second part, consisting of the following sections:</p>
<p>Our Faith</p>
<p>Catholic Bible, Catechism, Doctrine</p>
<p>Problems with the modern(ist) Church</p>
<p>Traditional Liturgy</p>
<p>Understanding Latin</p>
<p>Traditional prayer books, devotions, etc</p>
<p>Papal Encyclicals and related texts</p>
<p>Gregorian chant (CDs)</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>NOTE ABOUT THE SEARCH FUNCTION</strong>: The searched for terms will be highlighted in yellow throughout all the pages. If you are searching for a precise phrase (e.g. a book name) you can narrow down the results by putting the phrase into “quotation marks”. Then go to either of the book pages and scroll down through the text to see the highlighted phrases. If you can’t find the book you’re looking for submit a comment and I’ll try to help.</p>
<p>(An alternative way to search, on any particular page, is to press CTRL + F, which will bring up a search box where you can write in the word(s) – i.e. title or author. All matches will be brought up and highlighted.)</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><span style="text-decoration: underline;"><strong>Papal Encyclicals and related texts</strong></span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><a title="Papal Encyclicals Online" href="http://www.papalencyclicals.net/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Papal Encyclicals Online&nbsp;(www.papalencyclicals.net)</a> features encyclicals of 43 Popes (from 13th century to present) in html text as well as kindle format. The Vatican website also lists <a title="Vatican - papal documents" href="http://www.vatican.va/offices/papal_docs_list.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">encyclicals and other papal documents.</a></p>
<p>Some noteworthy texts:</p>
<p>Bl. Piux IX –&nbsp;<a title="The Syllabus of Errors - Pius IX" href="http://www.papalencyclicals.net/Pius09/p9syll.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">The Syllabus of Errors</a>&nbsp;(1864)</p>
<p>Bl. Pius IX –&nbsp;<a title="Quanta Cura - Pius IX" href="http://www.papalencyclicals.net/Pius09/p9quanta.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Quanta Cura</a>&nbsp;(1864, Condemning Current Errors)</p>
<p>Bl. Pius IX –&nbsp;<a title="Qui Pluribus - Pius IX" href="http://www.papalencyclicals.net/Pius09/p9quiplu.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Qui Pluribus</a>&nbsp;(1846, on Faith and Religion)</p>
<p>Bl. Pius IX – <a href="http://foretasteofwisdom.blogspot.de/2013/07/pope-pius-ix-iam-omnes.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Iam Vos Omnes</a> (1868, against Ecumenism)</p>
<p>St. Pius X – <a title="Pascendi Dominici Gregis - St. Pius X" href="http://www.papalencyclicals.net/Pius10/p10pasce.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Pascendi Dominici Gregis</a> (1907, on the Doctrine of the Modernists)</p>
<p>St. Pius X – <a title="Lamentabili Sane - St. Pius X" href="http://www.papalencyclicals.net/Pius10/p10lamen.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Lamentabili Sane</a> (1907, Condemning Errors of Modernism)</p>
<p><a title="Catechism on Modernism according to Pascendi Dominici Gregis of Pius X" href="http://archive.org/details/catechismonmoder00lemiuoft" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Catechism on Modernism according to the encyclical ‘Pascendi Dominici Gregis’ of His Holiness Pius X</a>&nbsp;(J.B. Lemius) – pdf, text, kindle format</p>
<p>St. Pius X – <a title="Vehementer Nos - St. Pius X" href="http://www.papalencyclicals.net/Pius10/p10law.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Vehementer Nos</a> (1906, Condemning Separation of Church and State)</p>
<p>St. Pius X –<a href="http://www.fisheaters.com/apostolicmandate.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Notre Charge Apostolique</a> (1910, against the Sillon movement)</p>
<p>St. Pius X – <a href="http://www.papalencyclicals.net/Pius10/p10moath.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">The Oath Against Modernism</a> (1910); or also <a href="http://www.saintsbooks.net/books/Pope%20St.%20Pius%20X%20-%20Oath%20Against%20Modernism%20-%209-1-1910.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">here</a></p>
<p>St. Pius V – <a title="Quo Primum - St. Pius V" href="http://www.papalencyclicals.net/Pius05/p5quopri.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Quo Primum</a>&nbsp;(1570, Promulgating the Tridentine Liturgy)</p>
<p>Paul IV – <a href="http://www.dailycatholic.org/cumexapo.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Cum Ex Apostolatus Officio</a> (1559, on the nullity of election and acts of heretical prelates)</p>
<p>Pius VI – <a href="http://novusordowatch.org/wp-content/uploads/piusvi-auctorem-fidei.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Auctorem Fidei</a>&nbsp;(1794, Condemning the Synod of Pistoia)</p>
<p>Pius XI – <a title="Quas Primas - Pius XI" href="http://www.papalencyclicals.net/Pius11/P11PRIMA.HTM" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Quas Primas </a>(1925, on the Kingship of Christ)</p>
<p>Pius XI – <a href="https://www.papalencyclicals.net/pius11/p11morta.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Mortalium Animos</a> (1928, against Ecumenism); also pdf <a href="http://sicutincaelo.org/downloads/MA_Read.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">here</a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p>—</p>
<p>Countless other classics on Church history, doctrine, lives and thoughts of saints and Church Fathers (including all the volumes of “Nicene and Post-Nicene Fathers” and “Ante-Nicene Fathers”) can be downloaded at <a href="http://www.ccel.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">ccel.org</a>. (The site unfortunately carries many Protestant books as well, so do your research to make sure any book you intend to read is Catholic and doctrinally sound.)</p>
<p>Other websites I recommend for free Catholic books: <a href="http://www.freecatholicebooks.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">freecatholicebooks.com</a>, <a href="http://www.saintsbooks.net/BooksList.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">saintsbooks.net/BooksList.html</a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://catholicebooks.wordpress.com/subject/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">catholicebooks.wordpress.com,</a>&nbsp;<a href="http://www.basilica.ca/elibrary" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">basilica.org/pages/ebooks.php</a>, <a href="https://isidore.co/calibre/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">isidore.co</a>, <a href="http://obrascatolicas.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">obrascatolicas.com</a>, (rare/out of print books in Portuguese, Spanish and English), <a href="http://liberius.net/langues.php" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">liberius.net/langues.php</a>&nbsp;(books in a dozen different languages).</p>
<p>For a vast quantity of texts, mostly in Latin, see&nbsp;<a title="Documenta Catholica Omnia" href="http://www.documentacatholicaomnia.eu/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">DocumentaCatholicaOmnia.eu</a>. &nbsp;The&nbsp;Vatican Library – digitized – is here:&nbsp;<a href="http://digi.vatlib.it/mss/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://digi.vatlib.it/mss/</a>.</p>
<p>If you know the name of the book, author or topic,&nbsp;<a href="http://archive.org/details/texts" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">archive.org/details/texts</a> and <a href="http://openlibrary.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">openlibrary.org</a> are also helpful.</p>
